`README.md`:

```md
# BamboozlEDR

A comprehensive ETW (Event Tracing for Windows) event generation tool designed for testing and research purposes. BamboozlEDR features a TUI interface and can generate realistic security events across multiple Windows ETW providers to test EDR detection capabilities, log analysis systems, and security monitoring solutions.

Note: This tool is built as a Proof-of-Concept. It is not polished code and it is intentionally built as a TUI utility that requires some user interaction to work. This limits the abuse by skiddies. 

## Features

###  ETW Provider Support
- **Microsoft-Windows-Antimalware** - Threat detection events (Event ID 48)
- **Microsoft-Windows-Antimalware-RTP** - Real-time protection events (Event IDs 27, 14)
- **Microsoft-Windows-LDAP-Client** - LDAP search and authentication events
- **Microsoft-Windows-TCPIP** - TCP/IP connection events
- **Microsoft-Windows-WMI-Activity** - WMI query and execution events (Event IDs 22, 11)
- **Microsoft-Windows-AMSI** - AMSI scan events
- **Microsoft-Windows-Defender** - Windows Defender events (Event IDs 5000, 5001, 1116, 1117)
- **Microsoft-Windows-DotNETRuntime** - .NET runtime events
- **Microsoft-Windows-Crypto-DPAPI-Events** - DPAPI access events
- **Microsoft-Windows-Security-Auditing** - Security audit events (Event ID 4688)
- **Microsoft-Windows-PowerShell** - PowerShell commandlet and AMSI events
- **Microsoft-Windows-RPC** - RPC function trace events (Event ID 14)
- **Microsoft-Windows-CodeIntegrity** - Code Integrity events (Event IDs 3023, 3036, 3076, 3077)
- **Microsoft-Windows-AppLocker** - AppLocker events (Event IDs 8003, 8004, 8006, 8007, 8021, 8022, 8024, 8025)
- **Microsoft-Windows-NTLM** - NTLM blocking events (Event ID 8001)

###  Event Generation Modes
- **Single Events** - Generate individual events for testing
- **Batch Events** - Generate multiple events from predefined lists
- **BamboozlEDR** - Execute multiple events simultaneously to confuse EDR
- **Buffer Overflow** - Generate unlimited high-volume events from all providers simultaneously
- **Custom Events** - Generate events with custom parameters

###  Security Features

#### String Obfuscation

All threat names in the data lists are obfuscated using XOR encoding to prevent them from appearing as plain text strings in the compiled binary. This protects against:
- Static analysis detection of threat names
- String-based signature matching
- Binary analysis tools finding embedded threat data

The obfuscation is applied at compile time and strings are deobfuscated only at runtime when needed, ensuring no plain text threat names exist in the binary file.

#### Administrator Privilege Checking
- **Conditional Feature Access** - ETW trace monitoring only available when running as administrator
- **Graceful Degradation** - Application works normally without admin privileges


### Main Menu Options

#### Standard Features (Available to all users)
1. **Microsoft-Antimalware-RTP** - Generate real-time protection events
2. **Microsoft-Windows-AMSI** - Generate AMSI provider events
3. **Microsoft-Windows-Antimalware** - Generate antimalware detection events
4. **Microsoft-Windows-AppLocker** - Generate AppLocker events
5. **Microsoft-Windows-CodeIntegrity** - Generate Code Integrity events
6. **Microsoft-Windows-Crypto-DPAPI-Events** - Generate DPAPI access events
7. **Microsoft-Windows-DotNETRuntime** - Generate .NET runtime events
8. **Microsoft-Windows-Ldap-Client** - Generate LDAP client events
9. **Microsoft-Windows-NTLM** - Generate NTLM blocking events
10. **Microsoft-Windows-PowerShell** - Generate PowerShell events
11. **Microsoft-Windows-RPC** - Generate RPC function trace events
12. **Microsoft-Windows-TCPIP** - Generate TCP/IP network events
13. **Microsoft-Windows-WMI-Activity** - Generate WMI activity events
14. **Microsoft-Windows-Windows Defender** - Generate Windows Defender events
15. **Cyber events** - Simulate cyber attack events
16. **BamboozlEDR** - Execute multiple events to confuse EDR
17. **Buffer Overflow** - Generate unlimited events from all providers
18. **User-Mode Antimalware Trace** - Monitor Microsoft-Antimalware-Engine (no admin required)

#### Administrator-Only Features
19. **NotMDE ETW Trace Monitor** - Create/manage external ETW trace session with the same providers MDE relies on.

### Detailed Provider Options

#### Microsoft-Windows-Antimalware
- **Single random malware event** - Generate one random malware detection
- **Single random benign event** - Generate one random benign detection
- **Spam malware events** - Generate multiple malware detections
- **Spam benign events** - Generate multiple benign detections
- **Ransomware** - Generate ransomware detection

#### Microsoft-Windows-Antimalware-RTP
- **RTP detection events** - Generate real-time protection detection events (27 + 14)

#### Microsoft-Windows-AMSI
- **Single AMSI event** - Generate AMSI scan event
- **Suspicious AMSI events** - Generate suspicious AMSI scans
- **Spam AMSI events** - Generate multiple AMSI scans

#### Microsoft-Windows-AppLocker
- **Process Audit (8003)** - Generate AppLocker process audit event
- **Process Block (8004)** - Generate AppLocker process block event
- **Script Audit (8006)** - Generate AppLocker script audit event
- **Script Block (8007)** - Generate AppLocker script block event
- **Appx Process Audit (8021)** - Generate AppLocker Appx process audit event
- **Appx Process Block (8022)** - Generate AppLocker Appx process block event
- **Appx Script Audit (8024)** - Generate AppLocker Appx script audit event
- **Appx Script Block (8025)** - Generate AppLocker Appx script block event
- **Spam AppLocker events** - Generate multiple random AppLocker events

#### Microsoft-Windows-CodeIntegrity
- **Revoked Driver (3023)** - Generate CiRevokedDriverNotLoaded event
- **Revoked Image (3036)** - Generate CiRevokedImageNotLoaded event
- **Policy Failure Audit (3076)** - Generate DeviceGuard policy failure audit
- **Policy Failure Block (3077)** - Generate DeviceGuard policy failure
- **Spam CodeIntegrity events** - Generate multiple random CodeIntegrity events

#### Microsoft-Windows-Crypto-DPAPI-Events
- **Single DPAPI event** - Generate single DPAPI access event
- **Spam DPAPI events** - Generate multiple DPAPI events
- **Infinite DPAPI events** - Generate DPAPI events continuously

#### Microsoft-Windows-DotNETRuntime
- **Single .NET event** - Generate .NET runtime event
- **Malicious .NET event** - Generate malicious .NET event
- **Spam .NET events (1337)** - Generate multiple .NET events

#### Microsoft-Windows-Ldap-Client
- **ADExplorer event** - Generate ADExplorer LDAP search
- **SharpHound events** - Generate SharpHound LDAP searches
- **Spam LDAP events** - Generate multiple LDAP searches

#### Microsoft-Windows-NTLM
- **NTLM Blocking Event (8001)** - Generate single NTLM blocking event
- **Spam NTLM events** - Generate multiple random NTLM blocking events

#### Microsoft-Windows-PowerShell
- **Single Random PowerShell event** - Generate single random PowerShell commandlet event
- **Random PowerShell AMSI event** - Generate random PowerShell AMSI scan event
- **Spam PowerShell events** - Generate multiple mixed PowerShell events

#### Microsoft-Windows-RPC
- **Function trace event** - Generate RPC function trace event (14)

#### Microsoft-Windows-TCPIP
- **Spam TCP/IP events** - Generate multiple network events
- **SMB Scan TCP/IP events** - Generate SMB scanning events
- **Single Random TCP/IP event** - Generate one random network event
- **Single Kerberos TCP/IP event** - Generate Kerberos network event
- **Single SMB TCP/IP event** - Generate SMB network event

#### Microsoft-Windows-WMI-Activity
- **Single WMI Event 22** - Generate WMI activity event
- **Suspicious WMI Events 22** - Generate suspicious WMI activity
- **Spam WMI Events 22** - Generate multiple WMI events
- **Single WMI Event 11** - Generate WMI event type 11
- **Suspicious WMI Events 11** - Generate suspicious WMI type 11
- **Spam WMI Events 11** - Generate multiple WMI type 11
- **Local WMI Event 11** - Generate local WMI event
- **Remote WMI Event 11** - Generate remote WMI event

#### Microsoft-Windows-Windows Defender
- **Realtime protection enabled (5000)** - Generate defender enabled event
- **Realtime protection disabled (5001)** - Generate defender disabled event
- **Malware detected + Remediated (1116/1117)** - Generate malware detection event
- **Spam Defender events** - Generate multiple defender events

### Buffer Overflow Mode (High-Performance)
The Buffer Overflow feature runs optimized ETW providers simultaneously at maximum throughput:

#### Performance Features:
- **Real-Time TUI Display** - Clean table interface showing statistics per provider
- **Live Statistics** - Success/failure counts, total events, and events per second
- **Advanced Performance Optimizations** - 100,000 pre-allocated GUID pool, reduced string conversions
- **Streamlined Event Generation** - Simplified event structures for maximum speed
- **6 Concurrent Providers** - Focused on highest-volume providers for optimal performance
- **Intelligent Logging** - Reduced frequency (every 1000 events) to minimize overhead
- **Cycle-Based Selection** - Efficient data cycling instead of expensive random generation
- **Auto-Refresh Display** - Updates every 2 seconds with current statistics
- **Enhanced Error Reporting** - Descriptive Windows error codes instead of cryptic numbers

## ðŸ”§ Technical Details

### ETW Provider GUIDs

- **Microsoft-Windows-TCPIP**: `2f07e2ee-15db-40f1-90ef-9d7ba282188a`
- **Microsoft-Windows-WMI-Activity**: `1418ef04-b0b4-4623-bf7e-d74ab47bbdaa`
- **Microsoft-Windows-AMSI**: `2a576b87-09a7-520e-c21a-4942f0271d67`
- **Microsoft-Windows-Crypto-DPAPI-Events**: `89fe8f40-cdce-464e-8217-15ef97d4c7c3`
- **Microsoft-Windows-PowerShell**: `a0c1853b-5c40-4b15-8766-3cf1c58f985a`
- **Microsoft-Windows-Security-Auditing**: `54849625-5478-4994-a5ba-3e3b0328c30d`

### Event Types and IDs
- **Antimalware Detection**: Event ID 48
- **Real-Time Protection**: Event IDs 27, 14
- **WMI Activity**: Event IDs 22, 11
- **Windows Defender**: Event IDs 5000, 5001, 1116, 1117
- **AppLocker**: Event IDs 8003, 8004, 8006, 8007, 8021, 8022, 8024, 8025
- **Code Integrity**: Event IDs 3023, 3036, 3076, 3077
- **NTLM Blocking**: Event ID 8001
- **RPC Function Trace**: Event ID 14

### Performance Optimizations
- **Pre-allocated GUID Pool**: 100,000 GUIDs for high-speed generation
- **Reduced String Conversions**: Optimized UTF-16 encoding
- **Streamlined Event Structures**: Minimal overhead event writing
- **Concurrent Provider Execution**: Parallel event generation
- **Intelligent Logging**: Reduced frequency to minimize overhead

`bof_sample/README_antimalware.md`:

```md
# Antimalware Events BOF

This Beacon Object File (BOF) generates fake Windows Defender/Antimalware detection events through ETW (Event Tracing for Windows). It mimics the functionality of the original Go-based antimalware tool but focuses specifically on ransom and random threat detection scenarios.

## Features

- **Mode 1**: Generate ransom detection events - Emits multiple ransomware-related threat detections
- **Mode 2**: Generate random threat detection event - Emits a single random threat detection from a predefined list

## Technical Details

- **Provider GUID**: `751ef305-6c6e-4fed-b847-02ef79d26aef` (Windows Defender Antimalware)
- **Event ID**: 48 (Antimalware detection event)
- **Channel**: 16
- **Level**: 2 (Warning)
- **Keyword**: `0x8000000000000000`

The BOF writes ETW events with 37 data fields matching the Windows Defender antimalware event schema, including:
- Threat information (name, GUID, SHA1)
- File paths and metadata
- Process information
- Detection timestamps
- Signature versions
- User context

## Compilation

Run the build script to compile the BOF:

```cmd
build_antimalware.bat
```

This will:
1. Detect your Visual Studio installation
2. Compile `antimalware_events.c` to `output/antimalware_events.obj`
3. Copy the aggressor script to `output/antimalware_events.cna`

## Usage in Cobalt Strike

1. Load the aggressor script:
   ```
   script-load output/antimalware_events.cna
   ```

2. Use the command:
   ```
   antimalware_events <mode>
   ```

### Examples

```
# Generate all ransom detection events
antimalware_events 1

# Generate a single random threat detection
antimalware_events 2
```

## Sample Threats

### Ransom Detection Events (Mode 1)
- Ransom:PowerShell/Roduk
- Ransom:Win32/CVE
- Ransom:MSIL/Gorf!pz
- Ransom:Win32/Blocker

### Random Threat Pool (Mode 2)
- VirTool:Win32/RemoteRegHiveCopy.B
- Behavior:Win32/RemoteRegDump.A
- Trojan:Win64/CobaltStrike.UFO!MTB
- Trojan:Win32/Wacatac.H!ml
- VirTool:MSIL/SoapHound.A

## Files Structure

```
bof_sample/

    â”œâ”€â”€ antimalware_events.obj    # Compiled BOF
    â””â”€â”€ antimalware_events.cna    # Copy of aggressor script
```

## Event Detection

These events will appear in:
- Windows Event Logs (Windows Defender Operational log)
- Microsoft Defender for Endpoint telemetry
- SIEM systems that collect Windows Defender events
- EDR solutions monitoring ETW events

## Security Considerations

This tool is intended for:
- Red team exercises
- Detection engineering
- Security tool testing
- Log analysis verification

Ensure you have proper authorization before using this tool in any environment.

## Based On

This BOF is based on the BamboozlEDR project's antimalware module, specifically implementing the "ransom" and "random" detection modes from the original Go implementation.

`bof_sample/antimalware_events.c`:

```c
#include <windows.h>
#include <evntprov.h>
#include <guiddef.h>
#include <objbase.h>
#include "beacon.h"

// Dynamic Function Resolution
DECLSPEC_IMPORT ULONG WINAPI ADVAPI32$EventRegister(LPCGUID ProviderId, PENABLECALLBACK EnableCallback, PVOID CallbackContext, PREGHANDLE RegHandle);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT ULONG WINAPI ADVAPI32$EventWrite(REGHANDLE RegHandle, PCEVENT_DESCRIPTOR EventDescriptor, ULONG UserDataCount, PEVENT_DATA_DESCRIPTOR UserData);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT ULONG WINAPI ADVAPI32$EventUnregister(REGHANDLE RegHandle);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT ULONG WINAPI ADVAPI32$EventActivityIdControl(ULONG ControlCode, LPGUID ActivityId);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT HRESULT WINAPI OLE32$CoCreateGuid(GUID* pguid);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT DWORD WINAPI KERNEL32$GetCurrentProcessId(void);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT int WINAPI MSVCRT$rand(void);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void WINAPI MSVCRT$srand(unsigned int seed);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT DWORD WINAPI KERNEL32$GetTickCount(void);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT LPVOID WINAPI KERNEL32$HeapAlloc(HANDLE hHeap, DWORD dwFlags, SIZE_T dwBytes);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT HANDLE WINAPI KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(void);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL WINAPI KERNEL32$HeapFree(HANDLE hHeap, DWORD dwFlags, LPVOID lpMem);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT VOID WINAPI KERNEL32$GetSystemTimeAsFileTime(LPFILETIME lpSystemTimeAsFileTime);

// Antimalware Provider GUID: "751ef305-6c6e-4fed-b847-02ef79d26aef"
static const GUID AntimalwareProviderGuid = {0x751ef305, 0x6c6e, 0x4fed, {0xb8, 0x47, 0x02, 0xef, 0x79, 0xd2, 0x6a, 0xef}};

// Threat data structure
typedef struct {
    char* threatName;
    char* detectionGuid;
    char* realPath;
    char* sha1;
} ThreatData;

// Sample ransom data
static ThreatData ransomData[] = {
    {"Ransom:PowerShell/Roduk", "5de2e73f-4009-7572-ddf7-2a6633b84ed2", "c:\\ImInYourLogs\\BamboozlEDR\\file_9569.exe", "415ea3a87ffb3e7316cda7e1e521a3c0bdbb135e"},
    {"Ransom:Win32/CVE", "8c027586-7f70-858f-4587-2bf17f3fb8f2", "c:\\ImInYourLogs\\BamboozlEDR\\file_38121.exe", "68bc54c82f20958223dffd1e1c8060b6917a2bbc"},
    {"Ransom:Win32/CVE", "0a481f71-277b-5cf2-f6f0-ded7f534e2b1", "c:\\ImInYourLogs\\BamboozlEDR\\file_58547.exe", "68bc54c82f20958223dffd1e1c8060b6917a2bbc"},
    {"Ransom:MSIL/Gorf!pz", "ef7e2045-c7bb-d16a-3dce-a2e2e2072d4f", "c:\\ImInYourLogs\\BamboozlEDR\\file_93396.exe", "bd7af32621f735bf12fe7b581c0a26d93d6a2125"},
    {"Ransom:Win32/Blocker", "ce77252c-7cf0-12b0-4f2b-8f6ae1bd8fe2", "c:\\ImInYourLogs\\BamboozlEDR\\file_51812.exe", "edbca22bd432b2f4ae36a997eb241ac531a3f586"}
};

// Sample threat data for random selection
static ThreatData threatData[] = {
    {"VirTool:Win32/RemoteRegHiveCopy.B", "ffd347f7-88fc-79b7-db59-b322429dd6f3", "C:\\Windows\\System32\\dpsVtevO.tmp", "2f9973ab4886b37964a449da52b45ea0cc49fef2"},
    {"Behavior:Win32/RemoteRegDump.A", "602b2c85-41a6-5bf5-357b-bf073865b9fc", "C:\\Windows\\System32\\kMNyWtTS.tmp", "02df4cbac806d14c9151d9be87670398f78825aa"},
    {"Trojan:Win64/CobaltStrike.UFO!MTB", "9ed08814-c936-23b7-dd50-737329f4198e", "D:\\bin\\data.dll", "5a75ff396fc5729cd1e5e960bd107185f1bf7f83"},
    {"Trojan:Win32/Wacatac.H!ml", "5e2ade39-1b75-9834-a39b-7ba40ffcb91b", "c:\\ImInYourLogs\\BamboozlEDR\\Desktop\\loader-1.dll", "07554158c6ba0cc84645b1d0b3a06c084c7c7dea"},
    {"VirTool:MSIL/SoapHound.A", "4e83a54a-aef1-ff2f-d653-3d2ff61e1e29", "C:\\Temp\\SOAPHound.exe", "d381decf2d999673df90490b4bd2a7d8d6cb218b"}
};

// Helper functions
int str_len(const char* str) {
    int len = 0;
    while (str[len]) len++;
    return len;
}

WCHAR* make_unicode(const char* ascii_str) {
    int len = str_len(ascii_str);
    WCHAR* unicode_str = (WCHAR*)KERNEL32$HeapAlloc(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, (len + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR));
    if (unicode_str) {
        for (int i = 0; i <= len; i++) {
            unicode_str[i] = (WCHAR)ascii_str[i];
        }
    }
    return unicode_str;
}

UINT64 get_current_time_as_filetime() {
    FILETIME ft;
    KERNEL32$GetSystemTimeAsFileTime(&ft);
    UINT64 result = ((UINT64)ft.dwHighDateTime << 32) | ft.dwLowDateTime;
    return result;
}

ULONG write_antimalware_event(REGHANDLE regHandle, ThreatData* data) {
    EVENT_DESCRIPTOR eventDescriptor = {0};
    eventDescriptor.Id = 48;
    eventDescriptor.Version = 0;
    eventDescriptor.Channel = 16;
    eventDescriptor.Level = 2;
    eventDescriptor.Opcode = 0;
    eventDescriptor.Task = 0;
    eventDescriptor.Keyword = 0x8000000000000000;

    // Constants
    UINT64 asSignatureUpdateTime = 133800893050000000ULL;
    char* asSignatureVersion = "1.421.1111.0";
    UINT64 avSignatureUpdateTime = 133800893020000000ULL;
    char* avSignatureVersion = "1.421.1111.0";
    UINT32 action = 2;
    UINT64 allowThreatExpirationUTC = 0;
    UINT32 blockThreatExecSubCategory = 0;
    char* classification = "0";
    char* detectionSource = "0x04000000";
    UINT64 detectionSourceHexInt32 = 0x04000000;
    UINT64 detectionTime = get_current_time_as_filetime();
    UINT64 engineUpdateTime = 133800893050000000ULL;
    char* engineVersion = "1.1.24090.11";
    BOOL isPassiveMode = FALSE;
    char* md5 = "8ac7a564d633c052ba19d40641410758";
    UINT64 platformUpdateTime = 133782115743760815ULL;
    char* platformVersion = "4.18.24090.11";
    UINT64 processCreationTime = 0;
    UINT32 processID = KERNEL32$GetCurrentProcessId();
    char* processPath = "Unknown";
    char* propertyBag = "NULL";
    char* remediationErrorCode = "0";
    char* resourceSchema = "file";
    char* schemaParamAndDataDelimiter = "|";
    char* schemaParamList = "SchemaParamFilePath";
    char* sha256 = "707ac8438648d54a2b1ecad0c30befd6a0542787d5f98da94c8cb440a287064b";
    char* sigSeq = "0247A7DE67260000";
    char* sigSha = "7dda9e0dc8a38822eacfe08e2a9f99946b65987f";
    char* threatTrackingId = "FC4FFBA8-FB4F-41AD-A8FD-07C0448AC531";
    char* user = "ImInYourLogsNow";
    char* userSid = "S-1-5-21-3133739513-2472346002-3133701003-501";
    INT32 wasExecutingWhileDetected = 0;
    BOOL isCritical = TRUE;

    // Convert strings to Unicode
    WCHAR* wSha1 = make_unicode(data->sha1);
    WCHAR* wSha256 = make_unicode(sha256);
    WCHAR* wMd5 = make_unicode(md5);
    WCHAR* wProcessPath = make_unicode(processPath);
    WCHAR* wThreatName = make_unicode(data->threatName);
    WCHAR* wRealPath = make_unicode(data->realPath);
    WCHAR* wUser = make_unicode(user);
    WCHAR* wUserSid = make_unicode(userSid);
    WCHAR* wResourceSchema = make_unicode(resourceSchema);
    WCHAR* wDetectionGuid = make_unicode(data->detectionGuid);
    WCHAR* wClassification = make_unicode(classification);
    WCHAR* wSchemaParamAndDataDelimiter = make_unicode(schemaParamAndDataDelimiter);
    WCHAR* wSchemaParamList = make_unicode(schemaParamList);
    WCHAR* wSchemaParamDataList = make_unicode(data->realPath);
    WCHAR* wRemediationErrorCode = make_unicode(remediationErrorCode);
    WCHAR* wSigSeq = make_unicode(sigSeq);
    WCHAR* wSigSha = make_unicode(sigSha);
    WCHAR* wThreatTrackingId = make_unicode(threatTrackingId);
    WCHAR* wPlatformVersion = make_unicode(platformVersion);
    WCHAR* wEngineVersion = make_unicode(engineVersion);
    WCHAR* wAsSignatureVersion = make_unicode(asSignatureVersion);
    WCHAR* wAvSignatureVersion = make_unicode(avSignatureVersion);
    WCHAR* wPropertyBag = make_unicode(propertyBag);

    if (!wSha1 || !wSha256 || !wMd5 || !wProcessPath || !wThreatName || 
        !wRealPath || !wUser || !wUserSid || !wResourceSchema || 
        !wDetectionGuid || !wClassification || !wSchemaParamAndDataDelimiter ||
        !wSchemaParamList || !wSchemaParamDataList || !wRemediationErrorCode ||
        !wSigSeq || !wSigSha || !wThreatTrackingId || !wPlatformVersion ||
        !wEngineVersion || !wAsSignatureVersion || !wAvSignatureVersion ||
        !wPropertyBag) {
        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_ERROR, "Memory allocation failed for Unicode conversion\n");
        goto cleanup;
    }

    // Create event data array - 37 fields as per the original
    EVENT_DATA_DESCRIPTOR eventData[37] = {0};
    
    // 1) Sha1 (string)
    eventData[0].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wSha1;
    eventData[0].Size = (str_len(data->sha1) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 2) Sha256 (string)
    eventData[1].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wSha256;
    eventData[1].Size = (str_len(sha256) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 3) MD5 (string)
    eventData[2].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wMd5;
    eventData[2].Size = (str_len(md5) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 4) ProcessID (uint32)
    eventData[3].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&processID;
    eventData[3].Size = sizeof(processID);
    
    // 5) ProcessCreationTime (uint64)
    eventData[4].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&processCreationTime;
    eventData[4].Size = sizeof(processCreationTime);
    
    // 6) ProcessPath (string)
    eventData[5].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wProcessPath;
    eventData[5].Size = (str_len(processPath) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 7) ThreatName (string)
    eventData[6].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wThreatName;
    eventData[6].Size = (str_len(data->threatName) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 8) RealPath (string)
    eventData[7].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wRealPath;
    eventData[7].Size = (str_len(data->realPath) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 9) WasExecutingWhileDetected (int32)
    eventData[8].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&wasExecutingWhileDetected;
    eventData[8].Size = sizeof(wasExecutingWhileDetected);
    
    // 10) Action (uint32)
    eventData[9].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&action;
    eventData[9].Size = sizeof(action);
    
    // 11) RemediationErrorCode (string)
    eventData[10].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wRemediationErrorCode;
    eventData[10].Size = (str_len(remediationErrorCode) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 12) DetectionTime (uint64)
    eventData[11].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&detectionTime;
    eventData[11].Size = sizeof(detectionTime);
    
    // 13) User (string)
    eventData[12].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wUser;
    eventData[12].Size = (str_len(user) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 14) UserSid (string)
    eventData[13].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wUserSid;
    eventData[13].Size = (str_len(userSid) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 15) ResourceSchema (string)
    eventData[14].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wResourceSchema;
    eventData[14].Size = (str_len(resourceSchema) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 16) DetectionGuid (string)
    eventData[15].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wDetectionGuid;
    eventData[15].Size = (str_len(data->detectionGuid) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 17) Classification (string)
    eventData[16].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wClassification;
    eventData[16].Size = (str_len(classification) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 18) SchemaParamAndDataDelimiter (string)
    eventData[17].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wSchemaParamAndDataDelimiter;
    eventData[17].Size = (str_len(schemaParamAndDataDelimiter) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 19) SchemaParamList (string)
    eventData[18].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wSchemaParamList;
    eventData[18].Size = (str_len(schemaParamList) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 20) SchemaParamDataList (string)
    eventData[19].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wSchemaParamDataList;
    eventData[19].Size = (str_len(data->realPath) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 21) DetectionSource (uint64)
    eventData[20].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&detectionSourceHexInt32;
    eventData[20].Size = sizeof(detectionSourceHexInt32);
    
    // 22) IsPassiveMode (bool)
    eventData[21].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&isPassiveMode;
    eventData[21].Size = sizeof(isPassiveMode);
    
    // 23) SigSeq (string)
    eventData[22].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wSigSeq;
    eventData[22].Size = (str_len(sigSeq) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 24) SigSha (string)
    eventData[23].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wSigSha;
    eventData[23].Size = (str_len(sigSha) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 25) isCritical (bool)
    eventData[24].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&isCritical;
    eventData[24].Size = sizeof(isCritical);
    
    // 26) ThreatTrackingId (string)
    eventData[25].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wThreatTrackingId;
    eventData[25].Size = (str_len(threatTrackingId) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 27) PlatformVersion (string)
    eventData[26].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wPlatformVersion;
    eventData[26].Size = (str_len(platformVersion) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 28) PlatformUpdateTime (uint64)
    eventData[27].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&platformUpdateTime;
    eventData[27].Size = sizeof(platformUpdateTime);
    
    // 29) EngineVersion (string)
    eventData[28].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wEngineVersion;
    eventData[28].Size = (str_len(engineVersion) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 30) EngineUpdateTime (uint64)
    eventData[29].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&engineUpdateTime;
    eventData[29].Size = sizeof(engineUpdateTime);
    
    // 31) ASSignatureVersion (string)
    eventData[30].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wAsSignatureVersion;
    eventData[30].Size = (str_len(asSignatureVersion) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 32) ASSignatureUpdateTime (uint64)
    eventData[31].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&asSignatureUpdateTime;
    eventData[31].Size = sizeof(asSignatureUpdateTime);
    
    // 33) AVSignatureVersion (string)
    eventData[32].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wAvSignatureVersion;
    eventData[32].Size = (str_len(avSignatureVersion) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 34) AVSignatureUpdateTime (uint64)
    eventData[33].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&avSignatureUpdateTime;
    eventData[33].Size = sizeof(avSignatureUpdateTime);
    
    // 35) BlockThreatExecSubCategory (uint32)
    eventData[34].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&blockThreatExecSubCategory;
    eventData[34].Size = sizeof(blockThreatExecSubCategory);
    
    // 36) PropertyBag (string)
    eventData[35].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wPropertyBag;
    eventData[35].Size = (str_len(propertyBag) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    // 37) AllowThreatExpirationUTC (uint64)
    eventData[36].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&allowThreatExpirationUTC;
    eventData[36].Size = sizeof(allowThreatExpirationUTC);

    ULONG status = ADVAPI32$EventWrite(regHandle, &eventDescriptor, 37, eventData);
    if (status == 0) {
        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "Antimalware event written successfully for: %s\n", data->threatName);
    } else {
        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_ERROR, "Failed to write antimalware event: %lu\n", status);
    }

cleanup:
    // Free all allocated Unicode strings
    if (wSha1) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wSha1);
    if (wSha256) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wSha256);
    if (wMd5) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wMd5);
    if (wProcessPath) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wProcessPath);
    if (wThreatName) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wThreatName);
    if (wRealPath) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wRealPath);
    if (wUser) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wUser);
    if (wUserSid) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wUserSid);
    if (wResourceSchema) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wResourceSchema);
    if (wDetectionGuid) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wDetectionGuid);
    if (wClassification) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wClassification);
    if (wSchemaParamAndDataDelimiter) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wSchemaParamAndDataDelimiter);
    if (wSchemaParamList) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wSchemaParamList);
    if (wSchemaParamDataList) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wSchemaParamDataList);
    if (wRemediationErrorCode) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wRemediationErrorCode);
    if (wSigSeq) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wSigSeq);
    if (wSigSha) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wSigSha);
    if (wThreatTrackingId) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wThreatTrackingId);
    if (wPlatformVersion) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wPlatformVersion);
    if (wEngineVersion) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wEngineVersion);
    if (wAsSignatureVersion) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wAsSignatureVersion);
    if (wAvSignatureVersion) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wAvSignatureVersion);
    if (wPropertyBag) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wPropertyBag);
    
    return status;
}

void mode_ransom_events() {
    BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "Emitting Antimalware ransom detection events...\n");
    
    REGHANDLE regHandle;
    ULONG status = ADVAPI32$EventRegister(&AntimalwareProviderGuid, NULL, NULL, &regHandle);
    if (status != 0) {
        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_ERROR, "Failed to register antimalware provider: %lu\n", status);
        return;
    }

    int ransomDataCount = sizeof(ransomData) / sizeof(ransomData[0]);
    for (int i = 0; i < ransomDataCount; i++) {
        GUID activityId;
        if (SUCCEEDED(OLE32$CoCreateGuid(&activityId))) {
            ADVAPI32$EventActivityIdControl(3, &activityId);
        }
        
        write_antimalware_event(regHandle, &ransomData[i]);
    }

    ADVAPI32$EventUnregister(regHandle);
}

void mode_random_threat_event() {
    BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "Emitting random Antimalware threat detection event...\n");
    
    REGHANDLE regHandle;
    ULONG status = ADVAPI32$EventRegister(&AntimalwareProviderGuid, NULL, NULL, &regHandle);
    if (status != 0) {
        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_ERROR, "Failed to register antimalware provider: %lu\n", status);
        return;
    }

    MSVCRT$srand(KERNEL32$GetTickCount());
    int threatDataCount = sizeof(threatData) / sizeof(threatData[0]);
    int randomIndex = MSVCRT$rand() % threatDataCount;

    GUID activityId;
    if (SUCCEEDED(OLE32$CoCreateGuid(&activityId))) {
        ADVAPI32$EventActivityIdControl(3, &activityId);
    }
    
    write_antimalware_event(regHandle, &threatData[randomIndex]);

    ADVAPI32$EventUnregister(regHandle);
}

void go(char* args, int len) {
    datap parser;
    BeaconDataParse(&parser, args, len);
    
    int mode = BeaconDataInt(&parser);
    
    switch (mode) {
        case 1:
            mode_ransom_events();
            break;
        case 2:
            mode_random_threat_event();
            break;
        default:
            BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "Usage:\n");
            BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "  Mode 1: Generate ransom detection events\n");
            BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "  Mode 2: Generate random threat detection event\n");
            break;
    }
} 
```

`bof_sample/antimalware_events.cna`:

```cna
beacon_command_register("antimalware_events", "Generate fake Windows Defender antimalware events", 
    "Usage: antimalware_events <mode>\n" .
    "  mode 1: Generate ransom detection events\n" .
    "  mode 2: Generate random threat detection event");

alias antimalware_events {
    local('$bid $mode $args $bof_path $bof_data');
    $bid = $1;
    $mode = $2;
    
    if ($mode eq "") {
        berror($bid, "Usage: antimalware_events <mode>");
        berror($bid, "  mode 1: Generate ransom detection events");
        berror($bid, "  mode 2: Generate random threat detection event");
        return;
    }
    
    # Try to find the BOF file in different locations
    $bof_path = "";
    if (-exists script_resource("antimalware_events.obj")) {
        $bof_path = script_resource("antimalware_events.obj");
    } else if (-exists "antimalware_events.obj") {
        $bof_path = "antimalware_events.obj";
    } else if (-exists "output/antimalware_events.obj") {
        $bof_path = "output/antimalware_events.obj";
    } else {
        berror($bid, "Could not find antimalware_events.obj BOF file!");
        berror($bid, "Make sure the BOF is in the same directory as the script or in an 'output' subdirectory");
        return;
    }
    
    # Read the BOF file
    $handle = openf($bof_path);
    if ($handle is $null) {
        berror($bid, "Could not open BOF file: " . $bof_path);
        return;
    }
    
    $bof_data = readb($handle, -1);
    closef($handle);
    
    if (strlen($bof_data) == 0) {
        berror($bid, "BOF file is empty or could not be read: " . $bof_path);
        return;
    }
    
    # Pack arguments
    $args = bof_pack($bid, "i", $mode);
    
    # Execute the BOF
    beacon_inline_execute($bid, $bof_data, "go", $args);
}

# Alternative function to load BOF from specific path
sub load_antimalware_events_bof {
    local('$bof_path');
    $bof_path = $1;
    
    if (!-exists $bof_path) {
        println("BOF file not found: " . $bof_path);
        return $null;
    }
    
    $handle = openf($bof_path);
    if ($handle is $null) {
        println("Could not open BOF file: " . $bof_path);
        return $null;
    }
    
    $bof_data = readb($handle, -1);
    closef($handle);
    
    if (strlen($bof_data) == 0) {
        println("BOF file is empty: " . $bof_path);
        return $null;
    }
    
    return $bof_data;
}

# Command to manually load BOF from specific path
beacon_command_register("antimalware_events_load", "Load antimalware events BOF from specific path", 
    "Usage: antimalware_events_load <path_to_bof>");

alias antimalware_events_load {
    local('$bid $bof_path $bof_data');
    $bid = $1;
    $bof_path = $2;
    
    if ($bof_path eq "") {
        berror($bid, "Usage: antimalware_events_load <path_to_bof>");
        return;
    }
    
    $bof_data = load_antimalware_events_bof($bof_path);
    if ($bof_data is $null) {
        berror($bid, "Failed to load BOF from: " . $bof_path);
        return;
    }
    
    # Store the BOF data globally for use by antimalware_events command
    global('$g_antimalware_events_bof');
    $g_antimalware_events_bof = $bof_data;
    
    blog($bid, "Successfully loaded antimalware events BOF from: " . $bof_path);
}

# Updated main command to use globally loaded BOF if available
alias antimalware_events {
    local('$bid $mode $args $bof_data');
    $bid = $1;
    $mode = $2;
    
    if ($mode eq "") {
        berror($bid, "Usage: antimalware_events <mode>");
        berror($bid, "  mode 1: Generate ransom detection events");
        berror($bid, "  mode 2: Generate random threat detection event");
        berror($bid, "");
        berror($bid, "If BOF is not found automatically, use: antimalware_events_load <path_to_bof>");
        return;
    }
    
    # Check if BOF is already loaded globally
    global('$g_antimalware_events_bof');
    if ($g_antimalware_events_bof !is $null && strlen($g_antimalware_events_bof) > 0) {
        $bof_data = $g_antimalware_events_bof;
    } else {
        # Try to find and load the BOF file
        if (-exists script_resource("antimalware_events.obj")) {
            $bof_data = load_antimalware_events_bof(script_resource("antimalware_events.obj"));
        } else if (-exists "antimalware_events.obj") {
            $bof_data = load_antimalware_events_bof("antimalware_events.obj");
        } else if (-exists "output/antimalware_events.obj") {
            $bof_data = load_antimalware_events_bof("output/antimalware_events.obj");
        }
        
        if ($bof_data is $null) {
            berror($bid, "Could not find or load antimalware_events.obj BOF file!");
            berror($bid, "Use: antimalware_events_load <path_to_bof> to manually load the BOF");
            return;
        }
    }
    
    # Pack arguments
    $args = bof_pack($bid, "i", $mode);
    
    # Execute the BOF
    beacon_inline_execute($bid, $bof_data, "go", $args);
}

println("Antimalware Events BOF loaded. Available commands:");
println("  antimalware_events <mode>     - Execute antimalware events BOF");
println("  antimalware_events_load <path> - Load BOF from specific path");
println("");
println("Modes:");
println("  1 - Generate ransom detection events");
println("  2 - Generate random threat detection event"); 
```

`bof_sample/beacon.h`:

```h
/*
 * Beacon Object Files (BOF)
 * -------------------------
 * A Beacon Object File is a light-weight post exploitation tool that runs
 * with Beacon's inline-execute command.
 *
 * Additional BOF resources are available here:
 *   - https://github.com/Cobalt-Strike/bof_template
 *
 * Cobalt Strike 4.x
 * ChangeLog:
 *    1/25/2022: updated for 4.5
 *    7/18/2023: Added BeaconInformation API for 4.9
 *    7/31/2023: Added Key/Value store APIs for 4.9
 *                  BeaconAddValue, BeaconGetValue, and BeaconRemoveValue
 *    8/31/2023: Added Data store APIs for 4.9
 *                  BeaconDataStoreGetItem, BeaconDataStoreProtectItem,
 *                  BeaconDataStoreUnprotectItem, and BeaconDataStoreMaxEntries
 *    9/01/2023: Added BeaconGetCustomUserData API for 4.9
 *    3/21/2024: Updated BeaconInformation API for 4.10 to return a BOOL
 *               Updated the BEACON_INFO data structure to add new parameters
 *    4/19/2024: Added BeaconGetSyscallInformation API for 4.10
 *    4/25/2024: Added APIs to call Beacon's system call implementation
 *    12/18/2024: Updated BeaconGetSyscallInformation API for 4.11 (Breaking changes)
 *    2/13/2025: Updated SYSCALL_API structure with more ntAPIs
 */
#ifndef _BEACON_H_
#define _BEACON_H_
#include <windows.h>

#ifdef __cplusplus
extern "C" {
#endif // __cplusplus

/* data API */
typedef struct {
	char * original; /* the original buffer [so we can free it] */
	char * buffer;   /* current pointer into our buffer */
	int    length;   /* remaining length of data */
	int    size;     /* total size of this buffer */
} datap;

DECLSPEC_IMPORT void    BeaconDataParse(datap * parser, char * buffer, int size);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT char *  BeaconDataPtr(datap * parser, int size);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT int     BeaconDataInt(datap * parser);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT short   BeaconDataShort(datap * parser);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT int     BeaconDataLength(datap * parser);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT char *  BeaconDataExtract(datap * parser, int * size);

/* format API */
typedef struct {
	char * original; /* the original buffer [so we can free it] */
	char * buffer;   /* current pointer into our buffer */
	int    length;   /* remaining length of data */
	int    size;     /* total size of this buffer */
} formatp;

DECLSPEC_IMPORT void    BeaconFormatAlloc(formatp * format, int maxsz);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void    BeaconFormatReset(formatp * format);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void    BeaconFormatAppend(formatp * format, const char * text, int len);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void    BeaconFormatPrintf(formatp * format, const char * fmt, ...);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT char *  BeaconFormatToString(formatp * format, int * size);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void    BeaconFormatFree(formatp * format);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void    BeaconFormatInt(formatp * format, int value);

/* Output Functions */
#define CALLBACK_OUTPUT      0x0
#define CALLBACK_OUTPUT_OEM  0x1e
#define CALLBACK_OUTPUT_UTF8 0x20
#define CALLBACK_ERROR       0x0d
#define CALLBACK_CUSTOM      0x1000
#define CALLBACK_CUSTOM_LAST 0x13ff


DECLSPEC_IMPORT void   BeaconOutput(int type, const char * data, int len);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void   BeaconPrintf(int type, const char * fmt, ...);


/* Token Functions */
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL   BeaconUseToken(HANDLE token);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void   BeaconRevertToken();
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL   BeaconIsAdmin();

/* Spawn+Inject Functions */
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void   BeaconGetSpawnTo(BOOL x86, char * buffer, int length);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void   BeaconInjectProcess(HANDLE hProc, int pid, char * payload, int p_len, int p_offset, char * arg, int a_len);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void   BeaconInjectTemporaryProcess(PROCESS_INFORMATION * pInfo, char * payload, int p_len, int p_offset, char * arg, int a_len);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL   BeaconSpawnTemporaryProcess(BOOL x86, BOOL ignoreToken, STARTUPINFO * si, PROCESS_INFORMATION * pInfo);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void   BeaconCleanupProcess(PROCESS_INFORMATION * pInfo);

/* Utility Functions */
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL   toWideChar(char * src, wchar_t * dst, int max);

/* Beacon Information */
/*
 *  ptr  - pointer to the base address of the allocated memory.
 *  size - the number of bytes allocated for the ptr.
 */
typedef struct {
	char * ptr;
	size_t size;
} HEAP_RECORD;
#define MASK_SIZE 13

/* Information the user can set in the USER_DATA via a UDRL */
typedef enum {
	PURPOSE_EMPTY,
	PURPOSE_GENERIC_BUFFER,
	PURPOSE_BEACON_MEMORY,
	PURPOSE_SLEEPMASK_MEMORY,
	PURPOSE_BOF_MEMORY,
	PURPOSE_USER_DEFINED_MEMORY = 1000
} ALLOCATED_MEMORY_PURPOSE;

typedef enum {
	LABEL_EMPTY,
	LABEL_BUFFER,
	LABEL_PEHEADER,
	LABEL_TEXT,
	LABEL_RDATA,
	LABEL_DATA,
	LABEL_PDATA,
	LABEL_RELOC,
	LABEL_USER_DEFINED = 1000
} ALLOCATED_MEMORY_LABEL;

typedef enum {
	METHOD_UNKNOWN,
	METHOD_VIRTUALALLOC,
	METHOD_HEAPALLOC,
	METHOD_MODULESTOMP,
	METHOD_NTMAPVIEW,
	METHOD_USER_DEFINED = 1000,
} ALLOCATED_MEMORY_ALLOCATION_METHOD;

/**
* This structure allows the user to provide additional information
* about the allocated heap for cleanup. It is mandatory to provide
* the HeapHandle but the DestroyHeap Boolean can be used to indicate
* whether the clean up code should destroy the heap or simply free the pages.
* This is useful in situations where a loader allocates memory in the
* processes current heap.
*/
typedef struct _HEAPALLOC_INFO {
	PVOID HeapHandle;
	BOOL  DestroyHeap;
} HEAPALLOC_INFO, *PHEAPALLOC_INFO;

typedef struct _MODULESTOMP_INFO {
	HMODULE ModuleHandle;
} MODULESTOMP_INFO, *PMODULESTOMP_INFO;

typedef union _ALLOCATED_MEMORY_ADDITIONAL_CLEANUP_INFORMATION {
	HEAPALLOC_INFO HeapAllocInfo;
	MODULESTOMP_INFO ModuleStompInfo;
	PVOID Custom;
} ALLOCATED_MEMORY_ADDITIONAL_CLEANUP_INFORMATION, *PALLOCATED_MEMORY_ADDITIONAL_CLEANUP_INFORMATION;

typedef struct _ALLOCATED_MEMORY_CLEANUP_INFORMATION {
	BOOL Cleanup;
	ALLOCATED_MEMORY_ALLOCATION_METHOD AllocationMethod;
	ALLOCATED_MEMORY_ADDITIONAL_CLEANUP_INFORMATION AdditionalCleanupInformation;
} ALLOCATED_MEMORY_CLEANUP_INFORMATION, *PALLOCATED_MEMORY_CLEANUP_INFORMATION;

typedef struct _ALLOCATED_MEMORY_SECTION {
	ALLOCATED_MEMORY_LABEL Label; // A label to simplify Sleepmask development
	PVOID  BaseAddress;           // Pointer to virtual address of section
	SIZE_T VirtualSize;           // Virtual size of the section
	DWORD  CurrentProtect;        // Current memory protection of the section
	DWORD  PreviousProtect;       // The previous memory protection of the section (prior to masking/unmasking)
	BOOL   MaskSection;           // A boolean to indicate whether the section should be masked
} ALLOCATED_MEMORY_SECTION, *PALLOCATED_MEMORY_SECTION;

typedef struct _ALLOCATED_MEMORY_REGION {
	ALLOCATED_MEMORY_PURPOSE Purpose;      // A label to indicate the purpose of the allocated memory
	PVOID  AllocationBase;                 // The base address of the allocated memory block
	SIZE_T RegionSize;                     // The size of the allocated memory block
	DWORD Type;                            // The type of memory allocated
	ALLOCATED_MEMORY_SECTION Sections[8];  // An array of section information structures
	ALLOCATED_MEMORY_CLEANUP_INFORMATION CleanupInformation; // Information required to cleanup the allocation
} ALLOCATED_MEMORY_REGION, *PALLOCATED_MEMORY_REGION;

typedef struct {
	ALLOCATED_MEMORY_REGION AllocatedMemoryRegions[6];
} ALLOCATED_MEMORY, *PALLOCATED_MEMORY;

/*
 *  version               - The version of the beacon dll was added for release 4.10
 *                          version format: 0xMMmmPP, where MM = Major, mm = Minor, and PP = Patch
 *                          e.g. 0x040900 -> CS 4.9
 *                               0x041000 -> CS 4.10
 *
 *  sleep_mask_ptr        - pointer to the sleep mask base address
 *  sleep_mask_text_size  - the sleep mask text section size
 *  sleep_mask_total_size - the sleep mask total memory size
 *
 *  beacon_ptr   - pointer to beacon's base address
 *                 The stage.obfuscate flag affects this value when using CS default loader.
 *                    true:  beacon_ptr = allocated_buffer - 0x1000 (Not a valid address)
 *                    false: beacon_ptr = allocated_buffer (A valid address)
 *                 For a UDRL the beacon_ptr will be set to the 1st argument to DllMain
 *                 when the 2nd argument is set to DLL_PROCESS_ATTACH.
 *  heap_records - list of memory addresses on the heap beacon wants to mask.
 *                 The list is terminated by the HEAP_RECORD.ptr set to NULL.
 *  mask         - the mask that beacon randomly generated to apply
 *
 *  Added in version 4.10
 *  allocatedMemory - An ALLOCATED_MEMORY structure that can be set in the USER_DATA
 *                     via a UDRL.
 */
typedef struct {
	unsigned int version;
	char  * sleep_mask_ptr;
	DWORD   sleep_mask_text_size;
	DWORD   sleep_mask_total_size;

	char  * beacon_ptr;
	HEAP_RECORD * heap_records;
	char    mask[MASK_SIZE];

	ALLOCATED_MEMORY allocatedMemory;
} BEACON_INFO, *PBEACON_INFO;

DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL   BeaconInformation(PBEACON_INFO info);

/* Key/Value store functions
 *    These functions are used to associate a key to a memory address and save
 *    that information into beacon.  These memory addresses can then be
 *    retrieved in a subsequent execution of a BOF.
 *
 *    key - the key will be converted to a hash which is used to locate the
 *          memory address.
 *
 *    ptr - a memory address to save.
 *
 * Considerations:
 *    - The contents at the memory address is not masked by beacon.
 *    - The contents at the memory address is not released by beacon.
 *
 */
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconAddValue(const char * key, void * ptr);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void * BeaconGetValue(const char * key);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconRemoveValue(const char * key);

/* Beacon Data Store functions
 *    These functions are used to access items in Beacon's Data Store.
 *    BeaconDataStoreGetItem returns NULL if the index does not exist.
 *
 *    The contents are masked by default, and BOFs must unprotect the entry
 *    before accessing the data buffer. BOFs must also protect the entry
 *    after the data is not used anymore.
 *
 */

#define DATA_STORE_TYPE_EMPTY 0
#define DATA_STORE_TYPE_GENERAL_FILE 1

typedef struct {
	int type;
	DWORD64 hash;
	BOOL masked;
	char* buffer;
	size_t length;
} DATA_STORE_OBJECT, *PDATA_STORE_OBJECT;

DECLSPEC_IMPORT PDATA_STORE_OBJECT BeaconDataStoreGetItem(size_t index);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void BeaconDataStoreProtectItem(size_t index);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void BeaconDataStoreUnprotectItem(size_t index);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT size_t BeaconDataStoreMaxEntries();

/* Beacon User Data functions */
DECLSPEC_IMPORT char * BeaconGetCustomUserData();

/* Beacon System call */
/* Syscalls API */
typedef struct
{
	PVOID fnAddr;
	PVOID jmpAddr;
	DWORD sysnum;
} SYSCALL_API_ENTRY, *PSYSCALL_API_ENTRY;

typedef struct
{
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntAllocateVirtualMemory;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntProtectVirtualMemory;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntFreeVirtualMemory;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntGetContextThread;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntSetContextThread;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntResumeThread;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntCreateThreadEx;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntOpenProcess;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntOpenThread;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntClose;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntCreateSection;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntMapViewOfSection;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntUnmapViewOfSection;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntQueryVirtualMemory;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntDuplicateObject;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntReadVirtualMemory;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntWriteVirtualMemory;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntReadFile;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntWriteFile;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntCreateFile;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntQueueApcThread;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntCreateProcess;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntOpenProcessToken;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntTestAlert;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntSuspendProcess;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntResumeProcess;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntQuerySystemInformation;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntQueryDirectoryFile;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntSetInformationProcess;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntSetInformationThread;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntQueryInformationProcess;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntQueryInformationThread;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntOpenSection;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntAdjustPrivilegesToken;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntDeviceIoControlFile;
	SYSCALL_API_ENTRY ntWaitForMultipleObjects;
} SYSCALL_API, *PSYSCALL_API;

/* Additional Run Time Library (RTL) addresses used to support system calls.
 * If they are not set then system calls that require them will fall back
 * to the Standard Windows API.
 *
 * Required to support the following system calls:
 *    ntCreateFile
 */
typedef struct
{
	PVOID rtlDosPathNameToNtPathNameUWithStatusAddr;
	PVOID rtlFreeHeapAddr;
	PVOID rtlGetProcessHeapAddr;
} RTL_API, *PRTL_API;

/* Updated in version 4.11 to use the entire structure instead of pointers to the structure.
 * This allows for retrieving a copy of the information which would be under the BOF's
 * control instead of a reference pointer which may be obfuscated when beacon is sleeping.
 */
typedef struct
{
	SYSCALL_API syscalls;
	RTL_API     rtls;
} BEACON_SYSCALLS, *PBEACON_SYSCALLS;

/* Updated in version 4.11 to include the size of the info pointer, which equals sizeof(BEACON_SYSCALLS) */
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconGetSyscallInformation(PBEACON_SYSCALLS info, SIZE_T infoSize, BOOL resolveIfNotInitialized);

/* Beacon System call functions which will use the current system call method */
DECLSPEC_IMPORT LPVOID BeaconVirtualAlloc(LPVOID lpAddress, SIZE_T dwSize, DWORD flAllocationType, DWORD flProtect);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT LPVOID BeaconVirtualAllocEx(HANDLE processHandle, LPVOID lpAddress, SIZE_T dwSize, DWORD flAllocationType, DWORD flProtect);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconVirtualProtect(LPVOID lpAddress, SIZE_T dwSize, DWORD flNewProtect, PDWORD lpflOldProtect);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconVirtualProtectEx(HANDLE processHandle, LPVOID lpAddress, SIZE_T dwSize, DWORD flNewProtect, PDWORD lpflOldProtect);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconVirtualFree(LPVOID lpAddress, SIZE_T dwSize, DWORD dwFreeType);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconGetThreadContext(HANDLE threadHandle, PCONTEXT threadContext);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconSetThreadContext(HANDLE threadHandle, PCONTEXT threadContext);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT DWORD BeaconResumeThread(HANDLE threadHandle);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT HANDLE BeaconOpenProcess(DWORD desiredAccess, BOOL inheritHandle, DWORD processId);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT HANDLE BeaconOpenThread(DWORD desiredAccess, BOOL inheritHandle, DWORD threadId);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconCloseHandle(HANDLE object);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconUnmapViewOfFile(LPCVOID baseAddress);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT SIZE_T BeaconVirtualQuery(LPCVOID address, PMEMORY_BASIC_INFORMATION buffer, SIZE_T length);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconDuplicateHandle(HANDLE hSourceProcessHandle, HANDLE hSourceHandle, HANDLE hTargetProcessHandle, LPHANDLE lpTargetHandle, DWORD dwDesiredAccess, BOOL bInheritHandle, DWORD dwOptions);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconReadProcessMemory(HANDLE hProcess, LPCVOID lpBaseAddress, LPVOID lpBuffer, SIZE_T nSize, SIZE_T *lpNumberOfBytesRead);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL BeaconWriteProcessMemory(HANDLE hProcess, LPVOID lpBaseAddress, LPCVOID lpBuffer, SIZE_T nSize, SIZE_T *lpNumberOfBytesWritten);

/* Beacon Gate APIs */
DECLSPEC_IMPORT VOID BeaconDisableBeaconGate();
DECLSPEC_IMPORT VOID BeaconEnableBeaconGate();

DECLSPEC_IMPORT VOID BeaconDisableBeaconGateMasking();
DECLSPEC_IMPORT VOID BeaconEnableBeaconGateMasking();

/* Beacon User Data
 *
 * version format: 0xMMmmPP, where MM = Major, mm = Minor, and PP = Patch
 * e.g. 0x040900 -> CS 4.9
 *      0x041000 -> CS 4.10
*/

#define DLL_BEACON_USER_DATA 0x0d
#define BEACON_USER_DATA_CUSTOM_SIZE 32
typedef struct
{
	unsigned int version;
	PSYSCALL_API syscalls;
	char         custom[BEACON_USER_DATA_CUSTOM_SIZE];
	PRTL_API     rtls;
	PALLOCATED_MEMORY allocatedMemory;
} USER_DATA, * PUSER_DATA;

#ifdef __cplusplus
}
#endif // __cplusplus
#endif // _BEACON_H_

```

`bof_sample/build_antimalware.bat`:

```bat
@echo off
setlocal enabledelayedexpansion

REM Try different Visual Studio paths
set "VCVARS_FOUND="

REM Check for VS 2022 Professional
if exist "C:\Program Files\Microsoft Visual Studio\2022\Professional\VC\Auxiliary\Build\vcvars64.bat" (
    set "VCVARS_FOUND=C:\Program Files\Microsoft Visual Studio\2022\Professional\VC\Auxiliary\Build\vcvars64.bat"
    goto :found_vcvars
)

REM Check for VS 2022 Community
if exist "C:\Program Files\Microsoft Visual Studio\2022\Community\VC\Auxiliary\Build\vcvars64.bat" (
    set "VCVARS_FOUND=C:\Program Files\Microsoft Visual Studio\2022\Community\VC\Auxiliary\Build\vcvars64.bat"
    goto :found_vcvars
)

REM Check for VS 2022 Enterprise
if exist "C:\Program Files\Microsoft Visual Studio\2022\Enterprise\VC\Auxiliary\Build\vcvars64.bat" (
    set "VCVARS_FOUND=C:\Program Files\Microsoft Visual Studio\2022\Enterprise\VC\Auxiliary\Build\vcvars64.bat"
    goto :found_vcvars
)

REM Check for VS 2019 Professional
if exist "C:\Program Files (x86)\Microsoft Visual Studio\2019\Professional\VC\Auxiliary\Build\vcvars64.bat" (
    set "VCVARS_FOUND=C:\Program Files (x86)\Microsoft Visual Studio\2019\Professional\VC\Auxiliary\Build\vcvars64.bat"
    goto :found_vcvars
)

REM Check for VS 2019 Community
if exist "C:\Program Files (x86)\Microsoft Visual Studio\2019\Community\VC\Auxiliary\Build\vcvars64.bat" (
    set "VCVARS_FOUND=C:\Program Files (x86)\Microsoft Visual Studio\2019\Community\VC\Auxiliary\Build\vcvars64.bat"
    goto :found_vcvars
)

:found_vcvars
if "%VCVARS_FOUND%"=="" (
    echo Visual Studio not found! Please install Visual Studio 2019 or 2022
    pause
    exit /b 1
)

echo Using Visual Studio at: %VCVARS_FOUND%
call "%VCVARS_FOUND%"

REM Create output directory
if not exist "output" mkdir output

REM Compile the BOF with minimal optimizations to avoid XMM issues
echo Compiling Antimalware Events BOF...
cl.exe /c /TC /GS- /Od /Oi- /Oy- /fp:precise /Gm- /GR- /EHs-c- /kernel /W3 antimalware_events.c /Fo:output\antimalware_events.obj

if %errorlevel% neq 0 (
    echo Compilation failed! Trying with different flags...
    cl.exe /c /TC /GS- /Od /Gm- /GR- /EHs-c- /kernel antimalware_events.c /Fo:output\antimalware_events.obj
    
    if %errorlevel% neq 0 (
        echo Compilation failed again! Trying minimal flags...
        cl.exe /c /TC /GS- antimalware_events.c /Fo:output\antimalware_events.obj
        
        if %errorlevel% neq 0 (
            echo All compilation attempts failed!
            pause
            exit /b 1
        )
    )
)

REM Copy aggressor script
copy antimalware_events.cna output\

echo.
echo Build completed successfully!
echo Files created:
echo   - output\antimalware_events.obj
echo   - output\antimalware_events.cna
echo.
echo To use in Cobalt Strike:
echo 1. Load the aggressor script: script-load output\antimalware_events.cna
echo 2. Use the command: antimalware_events ^<mode^>
echo    - antimalware_events 1    (ransom detection events)
echo    - antimalware_events 2    (random threat detection event)
echo.
pause 
```

`bof_sample/ldap_events.c`:

```c
#include <windows.h>
#include <evntprov.h>
#include <guiddef.h>
#include <objbase.h>
#include "beacon.h"

// Dynamic Function Resolution
DECLSPEC_IMPORT ULONG WINAPI ADVAPI32$EventRegister(LPCGUID ProviderId, PENABLECALLBACK EnableCallback, PVOID CallbackContext, PREGHANDLE RegHandle);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT ULONG WINAPI ADVAPI32$EventWrite(REGHANDLE RegHandle, PCEVENT_DESCRIPTOR EventDescriptor, ULONG UserDataCount, PEVENT_DATA_DESCRIPTOR UserData);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT ULONG WINAPI ADVAPI32$EventUnregister(REGHANDLE RegHandle);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT ULONG WINAPI ADVAPI32$EventActivityIdControl(ULONG ControlCode, LPGUID ActivityId);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT HRESULT WINAPI OLE32$CoCreateGuid(GUID* pguid);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT DWORD WINAPI KERNEL32$GetCurrentProcessId(void);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT int WINAPI MSVCRT$rand(void);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT void WINAPI MSVCRT$srand(unsigned int seed);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT DWORD WINAPI KERNEL32$GetTickCount(void);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT LPVOID WINAPI KERNEL32$HeapAlloc(HANDLE hHeap, DWORD dwFlags, SIZE_T dwBytes);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT HANDLE WINAPI KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(void);
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL WINAPI KERNEL32$HeapFree(HANDLE hHeap, DWORD dwFlags, LPVOID lpMem);

// LDAP Client Provider GUID
static const GUID LdapClientProviderGuid = {0x099614a5, 0x5dd7, 0x4788, {0x8b, 0xc9, 0xe2, 0x9f, 0x43, 0xdb, 0x28, 0xfc}};

// Simple helper functions
int str_len(const char* str) {
    int len = 0;
    while (str[len]) len++;
    return len;
}

void str_copy(char* dest, const char* src) {
    int i = 0;
    while (src[i]) {
        dest[i] = src[i];
        i++;
    }
    dest[i] = 0;
}

WCHAR* make_unicode(const char* ascii_str) {
    int len = str_len(ascii_str);
    WCHAR* unicode_str = (WCHAR*)KERNEL32$HeapAlloc(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, (len + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR));
    if (unicode_str) {
        for (int i = 0; i <= len; i++) {
            unicode_str[i] = (WCHAR)ascii_str[i];
        }
    }
    return unicode_str;
}

void make_random_string(char* buffer, int length) {
    char chars[] = "abcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyzABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZ0123456789";
    for (int i = 0; i < length - 1; i++) {
        buffer[i] = chars[MSVCRT$rand() % 62];
    }
    buffer[length - 1] = 0;
}

ULONG write_event(REGHANDLE regHandle, const char* searchFilter, const char* distinguishedName, const char* attributeList, DWORD processId, int iteration) {
    EVENT_DESCRIPTOR eventDescriptor = {0};
    eventDescriptor.Id = 30;
    eventDescriptor.Version = 0;
    eventDescriptor.Channel = 0x10;
    eventDescriptor.Level = 2;
    eventDescriptor.Opcode = 0;
    eventDescriptor.Task = 0;
    eventDescriptor.Keyword = 0x1;

    WCHAR* wSearchFilter = make_unicode(searchFilter);
    WCHAR* wDN = make_unicode(distinguishedName);
    WCHAR* wAttr = make_unicode(attributeList);
    
    if (!wSearchFilter || !wDN || !wAttr) {
        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_ERROR, "Memory allocation failed for event %d\n", iteration);
        goto cleanup;
    }

    ULONG scopeOfSearch = 0;
    ULONGLONG keyword = 0x1;
    
    EVENT_DATA_DESCRIPTOR eventData[6] = {0};
    eventData[0].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&scopeOfSearch;
    eventData[0].Size = sizeof(scopeOfSearch);
    
    eventData[1].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wSearchFilter;
    eventData[1].Size = (str_len(searchFilter) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    eventData[2].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wDN;
    eventData[2].Size = (str_len(distinguishedName) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    eventData[3].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)wAttr;
    eventData[3].Size = (str_len(attributeList) + 1) * sizeof(WCHAR);
    
    eventData[4].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&processId;
    eventData[4].Size = sizeof(processId);
    
    eventData[5].Ptr = (ULONGLONG)&keyword;
    eventData[5].Size = sizeof(keyword);

    ULONG status = ADVAPI32$EventWrite(regHandle, &eventDescriptor, 6, eventData);
    if (status == 0) {
        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "Event %d written successfully\n", iteration);
    } else {
        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_ERROR, "Failed to write event %d: %lu\n", iteration, status);
    }

cleanup:
    if (wSearchFilter) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wSearchFilter);
    if (wDN) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wDN);
    if (wAttr) KERNEL32$HeapFree(KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap(), 0, wAttr);
    
    return status;
}

void mode_random_events(int count) {
    BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "Emitting %d random LDAP Client search events...\n", count);
    
    REGHANDLE regHandle;
    ULONG status = ADVAPI32$EventRegister(&LdapClientProviderGuid, NULL, NULL, &regHandle);
    if (status != 0) {
        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_ERROR, "Failed to register provider: %lu\n", status);
        return;
    }

    MSVCRT$srand(KERNEL32$GetTickCount());
    DWORD processId = KERNEL32$GetCurrentProcessId();

    for (int i = 0; i < count; i++) {
        GUID activityId;
        if (SUCCEEDED(OLE32$CoCreateGuid(&activityId))) {
            ADVAPI32$EventActivityIdControl(3, &activityId);
        }

        char searchFilter[66];
        char distinguishedName[66];
        
        make_random_string(searchFilter, (MSVCRT$rand() % 55) + 10);
        make_random_string(distinguishedName, (MSVCRT$rand() % 55) + 10);

        write_event(regHandle, searchFilter, distinguishedName, "cn,sn", processId, i);
    }

    ADVAPI32$EventUnregister(regHandle);
}

void mode_adexplorer_event() {
    BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "Emitting LDAP Client ADExplorer search event...\n");
    
    REGHANDLE regHandle;
    ULONG status = ADVAPI32$EventRegister(&LdapClientProviderGuid, NULL, NULL, &regHandle);
    if (status != 0) {
        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_ERROR, "Failed to register provider: %lu\n", status);
        return;
    }

    GUID activityId;
    if (SUCCEEDED(OLE32$CoCreateGuid(&activityId))) {
        ADVAPI32$EventActivityIdControl(3, &activityId);
    }

    DWORD processId = KERNEL32$GetCurrentProcessId();
    
    write_event(regHandle, "objectGUID=*", "DC=i.am.in.your.logs,DC=now", "cn,sn", processId, 0);

    ADVAPI32$EventUnregister(regHandle);
}

void mode_sharphound_events() {
    BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "Emitting LDAP Client SharpHound search events...\n");
    
    REGHANDLE regHandle;
    ULONG status = ADVAPI32$EventRegister(&LdapClientProviderGuid, NULL, NULL, &regHandle);
    if (status != 0) {
        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_ERROR, "Failed to register provider: %lu\n", status);
        return;
    }

    DWORD processId = KERNEL32$GetCurrentProcessId();

    // Simplified set of SharpHound filters to avoid complex string issues
    char* filters[] = {
        "(objectClass=*)",
        "(objectclass=domain)",
        "member=*",
        "(objectClass=configuration)",
        "(samaccountname=*)"
    };
    
    int filterCount = 5;
    BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "Number of search filters: %d\n", filterCount);

    for (int i = 0; i < filterCount; i++) {
        GUID activityId;
        if (SUCCEEDED(OLE32$CoCreateGuid(&activityId))) {
            ADVAPI32$EventActivityIdControl(3, &activityId);
        }

        BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "Emitting searchFilter: %s\n", filters[i]);
        
        write_event(regHandle, filters[i], "DC=i.am.in.your.logs,DC=now", "cn,sn", processId, i);
    }

    ADVAPI32$EventUnregister(regHandle);
}

void go(char* args, int len) {
    datap parser;
    BeaconDataParse(&parser, args, len);
    
    int mode = BeaconDataInt(&parser);
    
    switch (mode) {
        case 1: {
            int count = 1338; // default
            if (len > 4) { // Check if there's more data
                count = BeaconDataInt(&parser);
                if (count <= 0) count = 1338;
            }
            mode_random_events(count);
            break;
        }
        case 2:
            mode_adexplorer_event();
            break;
        case 3:
            mode_sharphound_events();
            break;
        default:
            BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "Usage:\n");
            BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "  Mode 1: Generate random LDAP events [count]\n");
            BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "  Mode 2: Generate ADExplorer-like LDAP event\n");
            BeaconPrintf(CALLBACK_OUTPUT, "  Mode 3: Generate SharpHound-like LDAP events\n");
            break;
    }
}

```

`bof_sample/ldap_events.cna`:

```cna
beacon_command_register("ldap_events", "Generate fake LDAP events", 
    "Usage: ldap_events <mode> [count]\n" .
    "  mode 1: Random LDAP events (optional count, default 1338)\n" .
    "  mode 2: ADExplorer-like LDAP event\n" .
    "  mode 3: SharpHound-like LDAP events");

alias ldap_events {
    local('$bid $mode $count $args $bof_path $bof_data');
    $bid = $1;
    $mode = $2;
    $count = $3;
    
    if ($mode eq "") {
        berror($bid, "Usage: ldap_events <mode> [count]");
        berror($bid, "  mode 1: Random LDAP events (optional count, default 1338)");
        berror($bid, "  mode 2: ADExplorer-like LDAP event");
        berror($bid, "  mode 3: SharpHound-like LDAP events");
        return;
    }
    
    # Try to find the BOF file in different locations
    $bof_path = "";
    if (-exists script_resource("ldap_events.obj")) {
        $bof_path = script_resource("ldap_events.obj");
    } else if (-exists "ldap_events.obj") {
        $bof_path = "ldap_events.obj";
    } else if (-exists "output/ldap_events.obj") {
        $bof_path = "output/ldap_events.obj";
    } else {
        berror($bid, "Could not find ldap_events.obj BOF file!");
        berror($bid, "Make sure the BOF is in the same directory as the script or in an 'output' subdirectory");
        return;
    }
    
    # Read the BOF file
    $handle = openf($bof_path);
    if ($handle is $null) {
        berror($bid, "Could not open BOF file: " . $bof_path);
        return;
    }
    
    $bof_data = readb($handle, -1);
    closef($handle);
    
    if (strlen($bof_data) == 0) {
        berror($bid, "BOF file is empty or could not be read: " . $bof_path);
        return;
    }
    
    # Pack arguments
    if ($mode eq "1" && $count ne "") {
        $args = bof_pack($bid, "ii", $mode, $count);
    } else {
        $args = bof_pack($bid, "i", $mode);
    }
    
    # Execute the BOF
    beacon_inline_execute($bid, $bof_data, "go", $args);
}

# Alternative function to load BOF from specific path
sub load_ldap_events_bof {
    local('$bof_path');
    $bof_path = $1;
    
    if (!-exists $bof_path) {
        println("BOF file not found: " . $bof_path);
        return $null;
    }
    
    $handle = openf($bof_path);
    if ($handle is $null) {
        println("Could not open BOF file: " . $bof_path);
        return $null;
    }
    
    $bof_data = readb($handle, -1);
    closef($handle);
    
    if (strlen($bof_data) == 0) {
        println("BOF file is empty: " . $bof_path);
        return $null;
    }
    
    return $bof_data;
}

# Command to manually load BOF from specific path
beacon_command_register("ldap_events_load", "Load LDAP events BOF from specific path", 
    "Usage: ldap_events_load <path_to_bof>");

alias ldap_events_load {
    local('$bid $bof_path $bof_data');
    $bid = $1;
    $bof_path = $2;
    
    if ($bof_path eq "") {
        berror($bid, "Usage: ldap_events_load <path_to_bof>");
        return;
    }
    
    $bof_data = load_ldap_events_bof($bof_path);
    if ($bof_data is $null) {
        berror($bid, "Failed to load BOF from: " . $bof_path);
        return;
    }
    
    # Store the BOF data globally for use by ldap_events command
    global('$g_ldap_events_bof');
    $g_ldap_events_bof = $bof_data;
    
    blog($bid, "Successfully loaded LDAP events BOF from: " . $bof_path);
}

# Updated main command to use globally loaded BOF if available
alias ldap_events {
    local('$bid $mode $count $args $bof_data');
    $bid = $1;
    $mode = $2;
    $count = $3;
    
    if ($mode eq "") {
        berror($bid, "Usage: ldap_events <mode> [count]");
        berror($bid, "  mode 1: Random LDAP events (optional count, default 1338)");
        berror($bid, "  mode 2: ADExplorer-like LDAP event");
        berror($bid, "  mode 3: SharpHound-like LDAP events");
        berror($bid, "");
        berror($bid, "If BOF is not found automatically, use: ldap_events_load <path_to_bof>");
        return;
    }
    
    # Check if BOF is already loaded globally
    global('$g_ldap_events_bof');
    if ($g_ldap_events_bof !is $null && strlen($g_ldap_events_bof) > 0) {
        $bof_data = $g_ldap_events_bof;
    } else {
        # Try to find and load the BOF file
        if (-exists script_resource("ldap_events.obj")) {
            $bof_data = load_ldap_events_bof(script_resource("ldap_events.obj"));
        } else if (-exists "ldap_events.obj") {
            $bof_data = load_ldap_events_bof("ldap_events.obj");
        } else if (-exists "output/ldap_events.obj") {
            $bof_data = load_ldap_events_bof("output/ldap_events.obj");
        }
        
        if ($bof_data is $null) {
            berror($bid, "Could not find or load ldap_events.obj BOF file!");
            berror($bid, "Use: ldap_events_load <path_to_bof> to manually load the BOF");
            return;
        }
    }
    
    # Pack arguments
    if ($mode eq "1" && $count ne "") {
        $args = bof_pack($bid, "ii", $mode, $count);
    } else {
        $args = bof_pack($bid, "i", $mode);
    }
    
    # Execute the BOF
    beacon_inline_execute($bid, $bof_data, "go", $args);
}

println("LDAP Events BOF loaded. Available commands:");
println("  ldap_events <mode> [count] - Execute LDAP events BOF");
println("  ldap_events_load <path>    - Load BOF from specific path");

`bof_sample/ldap_events.cna-demo`:

```cna-demo
#
# LDAP Events Generator BOF - Fixed Version
#

# Global variables
global('$ldap_events_bof_path');

# Set the path to the BOF file - use absolute path or script_resource
$ldap_events_bof_path = script_resource("ldap_events.obj");

# Helper function to safely read BOF
sub read_bof_safe {
    local('$path $handle $data $size');
    $path = $1;
    
    # Check if file exists
    if (!-exists $path) {
        return $null;
    }
    
    # Get file size
    $size = lof($path);
    if ($size <= 0) {
        return $null;
    }
    
    # Read the file
    $handle = openf($path);
    if ($handle is $null) {
        return $null;
    }
    
    $data = readb($handle, $size);
    closef($handle);
    
    return $data;
}

# Main command handler - FIXED VERSION
alias ldap-events {
    local('$bid $mode $bof_path $bof_data $args');
    
    $bid = $1;
    $mode = $2;
    
    # Check if mode is provided
    if ($mode eq "") {
        berror($bid, "Error: Mode parameter is required");
        berror($bid, "Usage: ldap-events <mode>");
        berror($bid, "Available modes: random, single, sharphound");
        return;
    }
    
    # Validate mode
    if ($mode !in @("random", "single", "sharphound")) {
        berror($bid, "Error: Invalid mode '$mode'");
        berror($bid, "Valid modes: random, single, sharphound");
        return;
    }
    
    # Check BOF file path
    $bof_path = $ldap_events_bof_path;
    blog($bid, "Looking for BOF at: $bof_path");
    
    if (!-exists $bof_path) {
        # Try alternative paths
        $bof_path = "ldap_events.obj";
        if (!-exists $bof_path) {
            $bof_path = "./ldap_events.obj";
            if (!-exists $bof_path) {
                berror($bid, "Error: BOF file not found");
                berror($bid, "Tried paths:");
                berror($bid, "  " . $ldap_events_bof_path);
                berror($bid, "  ldap_events.obj");
                berror($bid, "  ./ldap_events.obj");
                berror($bid, "Current directory: " . cwd());
                return;
            }
        }
    }
    
    # Check file size
    local('$file_size');
    $file_size = lof($bof_path);
    blog($bid, "BOF file size: $file_size bytes");
    
    if ($file_size <= 0) {
        berror($bid, "Error: BOF file is empty or unreadable");
        return;
    }
    
    # Read BOF file using safe method
    $bof_data = read_bof_safe($bof_path);
    
    if ($bof_data is $null) {
        berror($bid, "Error: Failed to read BOF file");
        return;
    }
    
    if (strlen($bof_data) == 0) {
        berror($bid, "Error: BOF data is empty after reading");
        return;
    }
    
    blog($bid, "Successfully read BOF data: " . strlen($bof_data) . " bytes");
    
    # Pack arguments
    $args = bof_pack($bid, "z", $mode);
    
    # Execute the BOF
    blog($bid, "Executing LDAP Events BOF with mode: $mode");
    
    if ($mode eq "random") {
        blog($bid, "âš ï¸  Warning: This will generate 1338 events and may take some time");
        btask($bid, "Generating random LDAP events (this may take a while)...");
    } else if ($mode eq "single") {
        btask($bid, "Generating single LDAP event...");
    } else if ($mode eq "sharphound") {
        blog($bid, "ðŸ“Š Generating SharpHound-like LDAP events for detection testing");
        btask($bid, "Generating SharpHound LDAP events...");
    }
    
    # Execute with proper error handling
    try {
        beacon_inline_execute($bid, $bof_data, "go", $args);
        blog($bid, "BOF execution command sent successfully");
    } catch $error {
        berror($bid, "Failed to execute BOF: $error");
    }
}

# Test command to verify BOF loading
alias ldap-test-load {
    local('$bid $bof_path $bof_data');
    $bid = $1;
    
    $bof_path = $ldap_events_bof_path;
    blog($bid, "Testing BOF loading...");
    blog($bid, "BOF path: $bof_path");
    blog($bid, "File exists: " . (-exists $bof_path ? "Yes" : "No"));
    
    if (-exists $bof_path) {
        blog($bid, "File size: " . lof($bof_path) . " bytes");
        
        $bof_data = read_bof_safe($bof_path);
        if ($bof_data is $null) {
            berror($bid, "Failed to read BOF file");
        } else {
            blog($bid, "Successfully read " . strlen($bof_data) . " bytes");
            blog($bid, "First 20 bytes (hex): " . transform($bof_data, "hex", 20));
        }
    }
}

beacon_command_register("ldap-test-load", "Test BOF file loading", "");

# Convenience aliases
alias ldap-random {
    ldap-events($1, "random");
}

alias ldap-single {
    ldap-events($1, "single");
}

alias ldap-sharphound {
    ldap-events($1, "sharphound");
}

# Register commands
beacon_command_register(
    "ldap-events", 
    "Generate fake LDAP events for testing detection systems",
    "Usage: ldap-events <mode>\n" .
    "Modes:\n" .
    "  random     - Generate 1338 random LDAP search events\n" .
    "  single     - Generate a single LDAP search event\n" .
    "  sharphound - Generate SharpHound-like LDAP search events"
);

beacon_command_register("ldap-random", "Generate random LDAP events", "");
beacon_command_register("ldap-single", "Generate single LDAP event", "");
beacon_command_register("ldap-sharphound", "Generate SharpHound LDAP events", "");

# Initialization
on script_load {
    println("[+] LDAP Events BOF loaded");
    println("    BOF Path: " . $ldap_events_bof_path);
    
    if (-exists $ldap_events_bof_path) {
        println("    âœ… BOF file found (" . lof($ldap_events_bof_path) . " bytes)");
    } else {
        println("    âš ï¸  BOF file not found at: " . $ldap_events_bof_path);
        println("    Make sure ldap_events.obj is in the same directory as the .cna file");
    }
}
